  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_8f743023-cf92-4986-8f26-1c7dbab28cc6'
      });
    }

              <span id="reviewTextContainer987366808" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11231233890543763333"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: SPOILER-FREE ::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421636453i/13396560.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img width='100%' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405489811ra/10405299.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Exquisitely heart-wrenching and absolutely unputdownable, <i>Confess</i> is another unique Colleen Hoover masterpiece and one of the must-read books of this year!!</b><br/><br/>From the moment I read the blurb, I was intrigued by the story! And once I started reading, I discovered that there’s even more to this story than meets the eye. There’s an added layer to it that I absolutely loved but that I won’t mention because discovering it as you read is honestly best. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText11231233890543763333" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: SPOILER-FREE ::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421636453i/13396560.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img width="100%" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405489811ra/10405299.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Exquisitely heart-wrenching and absolutely unputdownable, <i>Confess</i> is another unique Colleen Hoover masterpiece and one of the must-read books of this year!!</b><br><br>From the moment I read the blurb, I was intrigued by the story! And once I started reading, I discovered that there’s even more to this story than meets the eye. There’s an added layer to it that I absolutely loved but that I won’t mention because discovering it as you read is honestly best. This review is spoiler free.<br><br>I can honestly say that this was the first time ever that a book made me completely break down crying (like real tears-pouring-down-my-face tears) in the very first chapter. The pain and loss and love were so achingly profound that I couldn't help but be overwhelmed by the emotions.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“How can a fifteen year-old-girl defend her love when that love is dismissed by everyone?”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>But, true to Colleen Hoover's amazing ability to make you feel a range of nearly every single human emotion possible, just a few pages later, I was laughing right out loud.<br><br>The story is about a heroine named Auburn who, by the age of 21, had already lost the most important thing in her life and was now just struggling to make ends meet. Faced with an impossible situation, she was desperate for any income she could get. When she came across a curious building, quite literally covered in scraps of paper with people's deepest, darkest confessions written on it, she had no idea what she'd find inside. She certainly wasn't expecting to find a quirky, ridiculously handsome, and very talented artist who practically begged her to work for him.<br><br>What she didn't know was that he was keeping a secret. He remembered her... knew her from before but couldn't tell her how. So the balance of their dynamic was very interesting as they both fell for each other while each respectively keeping back huge personal secrets that could change their lives...<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“They are the past and this is the present, and Auburn is… somehow both. She would be shocked if she knew how much of her past has affected my present, which is why I won’t be sharing the truth with her. Some secrets should never turn into confessions.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>I read this book as slowly as I could to prolong the experience. The story was completely unpredictable. Most books give you a vague idea of the direction they're heading in but not <i>Confess</i>. I read each page with no idea what would happen next and I honestly loved that about it. I have such complete trust in Colleen Hoover's writing that I never once doubted that she would take the story exactly wherever it needed to go. So I just sat back and enjoyed the ride!<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“I’m losing track of the lies I’m telling her, and lying to someone like her isn’t normally something I would do. But I don’t know how to tell her the truth…<br><br>I’ve never felt stronger than I feel when I’m with her. I’ve never felt like I had a purpose like I feel when I’m with her. I think about the first words I said to her when she showed up at my door. “Are you here to save me?”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br><br>True to CoHo style, <i>Confess</i> is completely different than anything else she's written. And, like I mentioned, there's an addition to the plot that added in just the perfect measure of heart-warming depth and heart-wrenching angst to the story. I loved the way it was introduced. It all felt so incredibly real.<br><br>One of the things I love most about Colleen Hoover's writing is how deeply she makes me care for her characters and how strongly she makes me feel for them. The opening chapter of this book (the one that had me break down crying) was the perfect representation of that because if she could make me feel that much for new characters in just a matter of pages, just imagine what she can do with an entire book.<br><br>While this book is certainly sexy, it's not overly steamy. However the circumstances of these characters' lives forced them to grow up fast, and this felt like a very mature book. The emotions and pure, raw intensity poured into even just a single kiss took my breath away over and over again.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“The more we kiss, the more we realize what we’re losing…He pulls back and looks me in the eyes with a pained expression. He moves his hand from the back of my head and brings it to my cheek, brushing a thumb over my bottom lip. “This already hurts.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>All in all, reading <i>Confess</i> was a truly magical reading experience. Because of all the layers in this story, there were actually three completely separate but intricately entwined storylines happening. I know that might sound a bit contradictory but it'll make perfect sense as soon as you read it. I promise. I felt fully and equally invested in all of them and couldn't wait to see how they'd all come together.<br><br>This book is most certainly a romance, but it's also so much more. It's a story of survival, courage, unexpected chances, fate, sacrifice, confessions, lies, love, and healing. It's deeply emotional and very fast paced. I flew through the pages and was unable to put it down.<br><br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>When he feels my tears falling against his chest, he doesn’t do anything to stop them. Instead, he simply holds me with a much tighter grip and presses his cheek against the top of my head…”I know, baby,” he whispers. “I know.”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>If you follow my blog, you'll know I'm a huge Colleen Hoover fan. I've loved everything she's ever written most especially because of the uniqueness of her stories and her ability to make me care so much for the characters. I feel like if she wanted to write a detailed account of the paint drying on her walls, I'd read it in a heartbeat. And I bet you she'd end up making me emotionally attached to that wall too!<br><br>Ooooh!! AND. This book has real artwork incorporated into it that was commissioned especially for <i>Confess</i>. As you read, you'll see these pieces inserted in the story in relevant places. In my advance copy, they weren't there yet but I read the descriptions of these paintings and I cannot wait to see them! <br><br>Guys, this book was truly fantastic. <br>Beautiful. Unique. Heart-wrenching. I LOVED IT!!<br><br><b> Rating: 5 stars! Standalone. </b><br>___________________________________________________<br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b></span>

<div id="review_1185572508" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1185572508" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1185572508?book_show_action=true">Jan 30, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2015">2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1185572508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9345295116503496677"><b>2 1/2 stars.</b> Erm. I think I have a love/hate relationship with Hoover's work. I keep coming back for more of her addictive writing style, despite having so many issues with her characters and slut-shaming. Though, I think it's official that I enjoy her far more when she's writing intriguing, possibly supernatural thrillers with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher' title='Tarryn Fisher' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tarryn Fisher</a>, than when she's writing contemporary romance. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24378015.Never_Never__Never_Never___1_' title='Never Never (Never Never, #1) by Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'>Never Never</a> is still my favourite. But <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22609310.Confess' title='Confess by Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'>Confess</a> is not too bad.<br/><br/>One of the things that almost always bugs me ab</span>
  <span id="freeText9345295116503496677" style="display:none"><b>2 1/2 stars.</b> Erm. I think I have a love/hate relationship with Hoover's work. I keep coming back for more of her addictive writing style, despite having so many issues with her characters and slut-shaming. Though, I think it's official that I enjoy her far more when she's writing intriguing, possibly supernatural thrillers with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5410816.Tarryn_Fisher" title="Tarryn Fisher" rel="nofollow noopener">Tarryn Fisher</a>, than when she's writing contemporary romance. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24378015.Never_Never__Never_Never___1_" title="Never Never (Never Never, #1) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Never</a> is still my favourite. But <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22609310.Confess" title="Confess by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Confess</a> is not too bad.<br /><br />One of the things that almost always bugs me about Hoover's novels is the way she characterizes her female protagonists. <b>They're bland, innocent, good girls and often victims</b>. They slut-shame other women, and when they start to behave in a flirtatious or sexual way themselves, we're treated to a piece of inner dialogue where they chastise themselves:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“What the hell am I doing? I don’t do this kind of thing. I don’t invite guys into my home.<br />Texas is turning me into a whore.”</b>
</i><br /><br />The annoying use of whore aside, what is this, the 1800s?<br /><br />Auburn Reed is another example of this. But I am prepared to admit that I think this is deliberate in a Bella Swan kinda way. Because Hoover is writing contemporary romance, I think she leaves her female protagonists deliberately open for interpretation so that her readers can imagine themselves in the story. I get it. I just don't really like it.<br /><br />There's also a bunch of the usual tropes. The guy (Owen) has had many girlfriends but Auburn is inexperienced. There's another total douche in the picture whose attempted sexual assault (yes, another one!) of Auburn is supposed to make Owen look better. Owen is flawlessly beautiful, not a blemish to be found:<br /><br /><i>
  <b>“...skin that looks so flawless, it makes me want to chase his father down and give him a high five for creating such an impeccable son.”</b>
</i><br /><br />I suppose these are all small bits and pieces. My real gripe is that I never really got a sense of the sexual/romantic chemistry between Auburn and Owen. There were many things about their relationship that I liked (and will talk about in a minute) but I never wanted them to be together, which is generally the whole point of a romance novel. Instead of roaring "YES!" when they slept together, I found myself wanting to skim read the sex scenes.<br /><br /><b>Okay. So there's all the negative. Now, I can talk about what I did like.</b><br /><br />Firstly, aside from his good looks, Owen seemed very different from other NA love interests. He was quirky, weird even, and a bit pretentious and hipster in a way that actually made him interesting, rather than annoying. I found his oddness charming. Secondly, there's a reveal about Auburn which I didn't see coming and thought was an unusual addition to a NA romance. I liked it.<br /><br />I also really like it when authors attempt to do something a bit different, especially in a genre that is defined by cliches and tropes. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17788403.Maybe_Someday__Maybe___1_" title="Maybe Someday (Maybe, #1) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Maybe Someday</a>, Hoover combined music and writing by releasing an album alongside the book with songs supposedly written by the characters. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22609310.Confess" title="Confess by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Confess</a>, Owen is an artist and there are some beautiful illustrations in the book. On top of the artwork itself, I really love the inspiration behind his art. He welcomes anonymous confessions in a dropbox at his art studio and his work is inspired by them. Very different.<br /><br />Owen was a very interesting character overall and it actually seems a shame that he was wasted on a romance novel where I didn't buy into their chemistry. Oh well, at least he had some great dialogue with Auburn.<br /><br />Definitely not a bad book, but I think I will wait for Hoover's less romancey novels. I'm still excited for <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24422492.Never_Never_Part_Two__Never_Never___2_" title="Never Never Part Two (Never Never, #2) by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Never Never: Part Two</a>.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://mycountryheart.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="9345295116503496677" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1139598436" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1139598436" />
    <a title="Angela" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30035966-angela"><img alt="Angela" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1523817330p2/30035966.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1139598436?book_show_action=true">Dec 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela" href="/user/show/30035966-angela">Angela</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=read-it-and-weep">read-it-and-weep</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30035966-angela?shelf=5-star-favorites">5-star-favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1139598436" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4017850925226009474"><b>"<i>OMG</i>"</b>... THIS BOOK!<br/><div>
<br/><b><i>THE NOTEBOOK</i>, <i>UGLY LOVE, </i></b><b><b><i>TFIOS,</i></b> AND <i>HOPELESS </i>HAD A SECRET LOVE CHILD! AND THAT LOVE CHILD IS <i>CONFESS.</i> </b><br/><br/>If you know anything about me then you know Colleen Hoover is my favorite author. If you don't know anything about me than that is pretty much all you need to know. She is the only author who has never let me down. <i>Confess </i>didn't let me down. I think Leah and I can both agree, the main thing we heard about this book was that it would induce tears within the first chapter.. An</div></span>
  <span id="freeText4017850925226009474" style="display:none"><b>"<i>OMG</i>"</b>... THIS BOOK!<br><div>
<br><b><i>THE NOTEBOOK</i>, <i>UGLY LOVE, </i></b><b><b><i>TFIOS,</i></b> AND <i>HOPELESS </i>HAD A SECRET LOVE CHILD! AND THAT LOVE CHILD IS <i>CONFESS.</i> </b><br><br>If you know anything about me then you know Colleen Hoover is my favorite author. If you don't know anything about me than that is pretty much all you need to know. She is the only author who has never let me down. <i>Confess </i>didn't let me down. I think Leah and I can both agree, the main thing we heard about this book was that it would induce tears within the first chapter.. And I had my doubts. <b>Ten pages in. I REPEAT TEN PAGES IN, I WAS A COMPLETE MESS. </b><br><br><i>Confess </i>follows the intertwining stories of Auburn and Owen. Both characters come from very separate yet equal backgrounds. Both facing more in the 20-something-years they've been alive than most will their entire lives. When <i>Confess </i>starts out right into Auburn's story you're more than likely, within the first few chapters, going to be thinking the same thing I was, "<i>Ha I got this whole thing figured out"</i>. Please don't think that. If you've ever read a Hoover book then you know you'd be a fool to think that (<i>yes I just called myself a fool, because God was I</i>).<br><br>Auburn is desperate for a second job when fate shines its face on her and she get offered one by Owen. When stopping in front of a studio covered in anonymous people's confession she never thought things would turn out the way they do. Both Auburn and Owen are perfectly written characters. Always revealing the perfect amount of themselves at the perfect time, always giving banter at the right moments, and always pulling out all the romantic stops at the right time<br><br><div>
<br><i><b>"I'm scared I'll never feel this again with anyone else," I whisper</b></i>
</div>
<div>
<br><i><b>He squeezes my hands. I'm scared you will."</b></i>
</div>
<br><br>I can't (<i>sadly) </i>say much more about them, because I know once I got started talking about them I wouldn't be able to stop!Then I would spill out all the wonderful things that make this book up! That being said I will tell you the spoil free things I loved about this book. There are four things that stole my heart and won me over. First, of course, the Art. When you think about pictures being included into a book you automatically think it'll be cheesy. It's not, it's a wonderful addition and takes this book to a level others wont reach. Second, the real readers confession that are sprinkled throughout this book and also fit so well with the art theme. Third, is the romance. It's Georgia peach sweet. And Four, well, you'll have to wait a minute for that one... Promise I'll get to it in a second.<br><br>When it came to plot, I had a lot of fear. I feared that with so much hype to this book that it would let me down. Then once the first chapter brought me to tears all I could think of was "<i>This book can only go down from here</i>"... All that was laid to rest. The plot starts strong, stays steady, and just when you're winding up on the end of the book and you're thinking <i>"ok that was great and all but what am I missing?"</i>; Colleen hits you right in the face with one of her famous big reveal. That brings you to my number four love. The ending. I <b>never ever </b>thought the story would end the way it did. Didn't think the story would come together and collide how she had it. The closer it got to the end the more I had to know what the ending was going to be. What the big secret was. I couldn't have been more happy with the ending! With everything perfect laid out, and the expression "somethings are better left unsaid" taking a whole new meaning, <i>Confess </i>will leave you wanting more.<b> It was perfect, amazing, and I don't think I took a single breath the whole last chapter. I constantly wonder if Colleen woke up one random morning and said "<i>you know what I'm going to be a writer</i>" or if she has always planned on becoming one... And I don't care, I thank the literary Gods every time she puts out a piece of work. </b>Not only does she give us something of her own, but the way she constantly finds away to shed light on others art as well... It's just astounding. <br><br><div>
<br><b><a href="http://4.bp.blogspot.com/-U6vyPom38ZU/VP-K8dumLwI/AAAAAAAABUk/zZvXm0iFEnY/s1600/confess.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426033623ra/13965491.gif" height="170" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a></b>
</div>
<br><br><b>1..2..3.. 5 OUT OF 5 "OMG" STARS <br></b>
</div></span>
  <a data-text-id="4017850925226009474" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review1139598436">

  <div class="left bodycol">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48477217-the-burning-rose-jess?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1614591809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1162824431422850342">5/5 stars.<br/>I have only one thing to say about this book: OMG! (only those who read the book will understand the connotation).<br/><br/>I don't like novels. Neither in books nor in movies, most of them simply surrounding around the couple, their love. There is usually nothing beyond.<br/>And that's what makes the amazing writer Colleen Hoover unique.<br/>Her books are far beyond just a love story.<br/>In this book there is also pain, there is another (non-romantic) love, there is laughter, there is sadness, there is reali</span>
  <span id="freeText1162824431422850342" style="display:none">5/5 stars.<br />I have only one thing to say about this book: OMG! (only those who read the book will understand the connotation).<br /><br />I don't like novels. Neither in books nor in movies, most of them simply surrounding around the couple, their love. There is usually nothing beyond.<br />And that's what makes the amazing writer Colleen Hoover unique.<br />Her books are far beyond just a love story.<br />In this book there is also pain, there is another (non-romantic) love, there is laughter, there is sadness, there is reality.<br />You see, in most love stories the reality is far from being realistic.<br />But in Colleen Hoover's books, there is a realistic love, something that can happen in real life, something that wasn’t meant to please the reader and for making a love story between a couple from “heaven”.<br /><br />This book got deep into my heart and soul.<br />The main characters in this book were just so touching and moving, that it's hard not to like them.<br />And the writing ... so unique, interesting, inviting. I think I fell in love with Colleen.<br /><br />So after reading the book in just a day and a half, I can give the book 5 stars here on the site, and million stars in my heart. I will definitely pick up this book in the future, and will read it again. <br /><br />Warmly and highly recommended. </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/987571859?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer987571859" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14417000313491503958"><b>5 OMG stars</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/785c7762-69c1-468d-8fe5-0662cc056e8c_zpsiavaccea.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426540949i/14043301.jpg' alt=' photo 785c7762-69c1-468d-8fe5-0662cc056e8c_zpsiavaccea.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Colleen Hoover is a genius. Every book of hers so different, and every one gets me right in the feels. <i>Confess</i> was no exception. If anything, this one hit me harder than many of her others. I can’t say it’s very often that I cry in the prologue of a book, but when you start out this way, it’s bound to happen…<br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/c7e1d6ea-3ab5-4c08-a82f-033f6bf987bc_zpsnmgei6n5.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426540949i/14043302.jpg' alt=' photo c7e1d6ea-3ab5-4c08-a82f-033f6bf987bc_zpsnmgei6n5.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I loved the confessions. I thought that was such a brilliant and unique idea for a story. To base it on real confessions. Things we have that are scary to put out there. I</span>
  <span id="freeText14417000313491503958" style="display:none"><b>5 OMG stars</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/785c7762-69c1-468d-8fe5-0662cc056e8c_zpsiavaccea.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426540949i/14043301.jpg" alt=" photo 785c7762-69c1-468d-8fe5-0662cc056e8c_zpsiavaccea.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Colleen Hoover is a genius. Every book of hers so different, and every one gets me right in the feels. <i>Confess</i> was no exception. If anything, this one hit me harder than many of her others. I can’t say it’s very often that I cry in the prologue of a book, but when you start out this way, it’s bound to happen…<br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/c7e1d6ea-3ab5-4c08-a82f-033f6bf987bc_zpsnmgei6n5.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426540949i/14043302.jpg" alt=" photo c7e1d6ea-3ab5-4c08-a82f-033f6bf987bc_zpsnmgei6n5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved the confessions. I thought that was such a brilliant and unique idea for a story. To base it on real confessions. Things we have that are scary to put out there. I loved the connections between the characters, the sacrifice, and the writing. <br><br>Most of all, I love how every thing became full circle in the end. EVERYTHING. This was a beautiful story that I won’t ever forget. And the art was just gorgeous. I was so happy I had the paperback at home as well as the kindle copy so I could look at both. <br><br>This story was real and raw and beautiful. It wasn’t perfect, the characters were flawed, but I love that too. I don’t want a story with perfect characters that make no mistakes. If you’re looking for a story that will grip you from the very start, make you laugh, make you cry, and make you FEEL, pick this one up! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/9f365c1e-c0c3-47e8-b939-f76de634bd8b_zpsngx1zche.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426540949i/14043304.jpg" alt=" photo 3bcbee7a-0391-4055-af6e-04be6c822258_zpsvhacjrod.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%207/024cd6a7-a190-4230-8ce5-75317450c84e_zpssfhoc9p7.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1232843029" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1232843029" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1232843029?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=death">death</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1232843029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10107584137086329955"><strong>This is the kind of New Adult book I enjoy reading.</strong><br/><br/>Confess wasn’t a shallow, cheesy or overdone story; it was deep, evocative, realistic and damn hard to put down. Usually, I get quickly bored if a contemporary read has a slow-kill-me-now pacing and, while this one definitely had it, <strong>I COULD NOT STOP READING</strong>.<br/><br/>I read everywhere. I read in the bus, during recess, in the car while going grocery shopping with my mom (she actually doesn’t mind it, but she keeps talking to me – she actually talks more </span>
  <span id="freeText10107584137086329955" style="display:none"><strong>This is the kind of New Adult book I enjoy reading.</strong><br /><br />Confess wasn’t a shallow, cheesy or overdone story; it was deep, evocative, realistic and damn hard to put down. Usually, I get quickly bored if a contemporary read has a slow-kill-me-now pacing and, while this one definitely had it, <strong>I COULD NOT STOP READING</strong>.<br /><br />I read everywhere. I read in the bus, during recess, in the car while going grocery shopping with my mom (she actually doesn’t mind it, but she keeps talking to me – she actually talks more when I’m reading) and <u>in class</u>. I don’t do that. I never do that. I even find it disrespectful for someone to be connected on Facebook, for example, when the teacher is speaking… yet, <strong>I just wasn’t able to turn off my tablet, put it aside, and continue living on without knowing what will happen to Auburn.</strong><br /><br />She got to me. Her story touched a part of my heart I had no idea could be affected. I wanted to strangle everyone that hurt her. I wanted to shield her from Trey, from Lydia, and help her get the happy ending she deserved. Because she did deserve for everything to turn out well for her. She might have appeared weak by moment but <strong>GOD DAMN</strong> the things she went through… and her need of keeping someone she loved close to her prevented her from doing whatever her heart desired but instead choose what felt <strong>RIGHT</strong> and <strong>SAFE</strong>. So it is very likely that you will be <u>frustrated</u> or <u>deceived</u> by her during your reading. Personally, <strong>I took those emotions and splashed them at the ‘‘villains’’ in the story.</strong><br /><br />Something I hate with New Adult stories is when they spotlight characters that are <strong>DESPERATE</strong> for romantic love, for a relationship, for sex and would do anything to get those things. Auburn was a woman that was willing to sacrifice so much for someone… that I cannot tell you about, and seeing her accepting to let go of Owen whom she was in love with and <em>treated her well</em>, in order to never lose that person in question (it might surprise you to discover who that is!) released my admiration.<br /><br />Circumstances made it that there was an insta-love between the two main protagonists from whom we actually have the point of views. I say ‘‘circumstances’’ because it seemed as if everything, when they first met, brought Auburn and Owen together and created a connection between them, including their sharing of a same middle name! Those were details but sometimes it’s the little details that can make a relationship between two people look firmer than any other one.<br /><br />Oh, how I loved the writing. Beautiful, smooth… ❤<br /><br /><strong>I always thought Colleen Hoover to be way too overrated… but, believe me, I’m taking that thought back.</strong><br /><br />PS. The paintings were completely stunning!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10107584137086329955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1256224555" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1256224555" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1256224555?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1256224555" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9781237061449172167">You know that a book will haunt you for a very long time when it brings you tears from the very first pages.<b>I finally understand the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover' title='Colleen Hoover' rel='nofollow noopener'>Colleen Hoover</a> hype.She is totally worth it.</b> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439384952i/15828739.jpg' width='300' height='350' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Hopefully,she has more than one fate,Owen.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br/>Probably not one of the most popular quotes,but it touches the essence of this <b>extremely beautiful and heartbreaking story</b>.Fate was cruel and brutal to both Owen and Auburn,but they were given a second chance in happiness when they met.And then,they were torn apart.A</span>
  <span id="freeText9781237061449172167" style="display:none">You know that a book will haunt you for a very long time when it brings you tears from the very first pages.<b>I finally understand the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5430144.Colleen_Hoover" title="Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Colleen Hoover</a> hype.She is totally worth it.</b> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1439384952i/15828739.jpg" width="300" height="350" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>Hopefully,she has more than one fate,Owen.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Probably not one of the most popular quotes,but it touches the essence of this <b>extremely beautiful and heartbreaking story</b>.Fate was cruel and brutal to both Owen and Auburn,but they were given a second chance in happiness when they met.And then,they were torn apart.Auburn had some priorities,and a relationship with Owen could jeopardize everything she fought for all these years.She silenced her heart,but it was not enough,because when she was with him,she felt like someone truly found her.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I'm afraid if I listen to my heart once,I'll never figure out how to ignore it again.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>I don't think I would be able to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22609310.Confess" title="Confess by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Confess</a> again.Not because it wasn't a <b>gem</b>,but exactly because it was.Every page,every sentence hold <b>pain,a gut-wrenching,lifesucking pain</b>.I lost count of the times I was on the verge of tears and I could taste bile in my mouth.It <b>consumed me</b> in a unique way,I wanted so badly to right the things that went wrong,to kill Trey and Lydia with my bare hands,to align the stars in the sky so that Owen and Auburn would end up together.I swam in a sea full of emotions and despair,I was struggling to reach the surface with every breath I had left,and then I kept thinking that if I felt this way about a secondhand experience,then Owen and Auburn are some of the strongest protagonists I had ever met.<br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>There are people you meet that you get to know,and then there are people you meet that you already know.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>Owen and Auburn are two characters I came to love deeply.Their lifes were messy and they had not complete control over them.Auburn was treated horribly by the same people she tried to appease,a tragedy was tattooed in her soul,yet she found the courage to love fiercely.Owen expressed himself through art,but he had to confess his sins and take the blame for sins he didn't even commit,to help his father become a father again and to show Auburn that she was a wonderful person who deserved a lot more.She deserved <i>him</i>.And I deserved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/22609310.Confess" title="Confess by Colleen Hoover" rel="nofollow noopener">Confess</a>.And you deserve it.<i>Every reader deserves it.</i><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>I’ll love you forever.Even when I can’t.</blockquote>
  </i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="9781237061449172167" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1223777166" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1223777166" />
    <a title="Geri Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads"><img alt="Geri Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487874758p2/11757728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1223777166?book_show_action=true">Mar 10, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Geri Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Geri Reads" href="/user/show/11757728-geri-reads">Geri Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/22667115-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1223777166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5940341869558088936">No one could accuse Colleen Hoover for not being creative with every single thing she's released thus far. She always has a knack of infusing something unique to her books from poetry, to songs, to plot twist. In this book, it was art. They were beautiful. The way she used the confessions with the art was very unique. They were the best part of the book for me.<br/><br/>Unfortunately, the rest left me underwhelmed. <br/><br/><a href='http://tinypic.com?ref=2s10whw' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426146205i/13980567.png' alt='Image and video hosting by TinyPic' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I have no problem with cliches or whatever as long as I am able to relate to the charac</span>
  <span id="freeText5940341869558088936" style="display:none">No one could accuse Colleen Hoover for not being creative with every single thing she's released thus far. She always has a knack of infusing something unique to her books from poetry, to songs, to plot twist. In this book, it was art. They were beautiful. The way she used the confessions with the art was very unique. They were the best part of the book for me.<br><br>Unfortunately, the rest left me underwhelmed. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2s10whw" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426146205i/13980567.png" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I have no problem with cliches or whatever as long as I am able to relate to the characters. Sadly, Owen and Auburn left me cold. I couldn't find anything remotely interesting about them. Sure their lives are fucked up and they suffered tremendous tragedies in their young lives...but most characters in this genre often have tragic pasts so they don't automatically make me feel sympathetic anymore. What keeps me interested is how the characters deal with their tragedies. <br><br>In this book, it was a big fail. At least for me. I feel for Auburn somewhat. Her situation wasn't an easy one for sure. But I wasn't impressed with the fact that she only grew a backbone AFTER she met Owen. Prior to that, she just moved with the flow. It was as if her life didn't start until she met Owen. She wasn't sure what she wants to do or even what she likes. She's only doing <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ the hair thing because of her son <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but even then, her attitude was all, "Poor me, I have no talent and I suck at being a hairdresser. Poor me." I do understand. Her choices were fairly limited but her whole attitude was off putting. <br><br><blockquote>“I suck at cutting hair. I hate listening to everyone’s problems while they sit in the salon chair. I swear, people take so many things for granted, and hearing all their whiny stories puts me in such a bad mood.”</blockquote><br><i>Oh, the irony.</i><br><br><blockquote>“There are a few really good clients. People I look forward to. I think it’s not so much the people that I don’t like, but the fact that I had to choose something I didn’t want to do.”</blockquote><br><br>And when Owen told her about how his art chose him, she thought...<br><br><blockquote>I love that answer. I’m also jealous of it, because I wish I could have been born with a natural talent. Something that would have chosen me, so that I wouldn’t have to cut hair all day.</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=34ys36t" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980568.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Owen gave me the heebei jeebeis- ...and he didn't get better. It only got better after I realized 'Gosh, he's the hero! Of course, it's perfectly fine to act possessive towards a girl he just met. Silly me.' <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=hrhixs" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980569.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>No worries though, there's always Trey (the token douchenozzle) to pin my righteous anger on. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=b3mkqe" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980570.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I wanted him to disappear. The fact that he's everywhere annoyed me. The fact that he and Auburn seems to have more page time together was disappointing. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2wd66ir" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980571.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It didn't help that I didn't feel any connection between Owen and Auburn. They saw each other and boom--a day later they are obsessed, in love or whatever. I couldn't handle it. There was no build up to their romance whatsoever. I kept being told 'This happened' and 'I felt this for her/him' but I wasn't shown. Of course, the last 2% of the book 'explained' how they're connected but even then, it still didn't make sense to me.<br><br>Maybe I'm getting too old for these types of "fated to be together" stories...because I didn't find anything remotely romantic about their connection. When I got to that part, I was like...<br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=10dgt8g" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980572.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>It was cute. Very cute. But my cynical heart wasn't a bit persuaded. <br><br><a href="http://tinypic.com?ref=2qscdmr" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1426146205ra/13980573.gif" alt="Image and video hosting by TinyPic" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Or...<br><br>Never mind. <br><br>Sorry, CoHo. I still love you but this one wasn't my cuppa.<br><br>EDIT: Trigger warning. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ There's a scene where Trey sexually attacked Auburn. He would have raped her had her roommate didn't stop him. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="5940341869558088936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988431880?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy | Foxy Blogs" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy | Foxy Blogs" href="/user/show/9955253-amy-foxy-blogs">Amy | Foxy Blogs</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2035894682154859411"><b>Oh, em, gee!!!</b> FIVE STARS!<br/><br/><i> Finding your heart somewhere between the <u>truth and lies</u>. </i><br/><br/><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Owen</u>
</b><br/>Owen’s dad is a lawyer<br/>Owen has a cat named Owen<br/>Owen has only 2 phone numbers in his phone<br/><br/><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Auburn</u>
</b><br/>Auburn gave Owen a drunken haircut<br/>Auburn grew up in Portland, Oregon<br/>Auburn has a roommate named Emory <br/><br/><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Confess</u>
</b><br/>The horror movie 1408 is mentioned<br/>The story is broken into 3 parts<br/>Two states play a major role in this story<br/><br/>I have a <b>conf</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2035894682154859411" style="display:none"><b>Oh, em, gee!!!</b> FIVE STARS!<br><br><i> Finding your heart somewhere between the <u>truth and lies</u>. </i><br><br><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Owen</u>
</b><br>Owen’s dad is a lawyer<br>Owen has a cat named Owen<br>Owen has only 2 phone numbers in his phone<br><br><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Auburn</u>
</b><br>Auburn gave Owen a drunken haircut<br>Auburn grew up in Portland, Oregon<br>Auburn has a roommate named Emory <br><br><b>
  <u>2 truths and a lie about Confess</u>
</b><br>The horror movie 1408 is mentioned<br>The story is broken into 3 parts<br>Two states play a major role in this story<br><br>I have a <b>confession</b>-&gt; out of the 9 things mentioned above 7 are true and 2 are lies. Have fun figuring out which ones are the lies and which ones are the truths. :)<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1425614383i/13911864._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>While reading this book I had to keep stopping to tell my husband what a great book I was reading. And then, throughout the day, I would give him an update on what was happening in the book. When he arrived home tonight he asked me if I had finished my book. I wonder if he’ll miss hearing me talk about the book or if he was checking to see if I’ve come back to reality. *lol*<br><br>The dedication is was what prompted me to tell my husband about <b>Confess</b>: <br><br><b>The confessions you read within this novel are true confessions, submitted anonymously by readers. This book is dedicated to all of you who found the courage to share them. </b><br><br>Whoa! That dedication intrigued me. Then the first confession left me with my mouth hanging up. It still haunts me to think about it. I have so many questions for this anonymous person. I suppose that will be one confession that goes to the grave with the person. Actually, all the confessions were fascinating and left me pondering the person behind the secret. <br><br>CoHo is one of my favorite authors. When I open her books I know I’m in for something special. Her stories challenge me to think outside the box. My first CoHo experience was with Slammed. I had never even heard of Slammed poetry prior to reading that book. I had the same experience with this book… the concept in this book with the confessions was a brilliant idea. I LOVED IT!!! I want to live in CoHo’s brain and figure out where she gets all these awesome ideas. <br><br>Also <b>CONFESS</b> includes original artwork by Danny O’Connor to augment your reading experience! <i>As an arc it didn't include the artwork. I'm looking forward to the published version so I can view his artwork.</i> I love how CoHo enhances your reading by offering <b>more</b> to her stories... like in Maybe Someday it had music that accompanied the story. <br><br>I don’t want to elaborate too much on the story line because something's are best experienced on your own. <br><br><b>RELEASE DATE: 3/10/2015</b><br>Pre-order | order: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/1kuzOFq">http://amzn.to/1kuzOFq</a><br><br><b>STANDALONE</b><br><br>**Complimentary copy in exchange for an honest review.**<br><br><a href="http://foxyblogs.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1408724793i/10887518.png" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1014433763" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1014433763" />
    <a title="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei"><img alt="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421992465p2/2551178.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1014433763?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lady Vigilante (Feifei)" href="/user/show/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei">Lady Vigilante (Feifei)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=what-are-you-trying-to-say">what-are-you-trying-to-say</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=third-time-s-the-charm-romance">third-time-s-the-charm-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=sweet-hero">sweet-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=new-adult-express">new-adult-express</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=contemporary-duckie">contemporary-duckie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=i-trust-my-friends">i-trust-my-friends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=cheese-puffs">cheese-puffs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2551178-lady-vigilante-feifei?shelf=choke-dat-ho">choke-dat-ho</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1014433763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11903215425086248477"><b>3 stars overall, but with <i>many</i> 2 star moments that were only balanced out by the occasional but memorable 4-5 star parts</b><br/><br/>I feel like the first thing I need to say here is that I didn’t hate this book. Yes, there were many parts that were hard for me to read and made me angry but overall I did like it. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426019307i/13963325.jpg' width='250' height='350' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>See that picture of my Confess paperback up there with all the orange sticky-notes? Half of them bookmarked a scene where I was about to chuck the book at my wall because the characters were so frus</span>
  <span id="freeText11903215425086248477" style="display:none"><b>3 stars overall, but with <i>many</i> 2 star moments that were only balanced out by the occasional but memorable 4-5 star parts</b><br><br>I feel like the first thing I need to say here is that I didn’t hate this book. Yes, there were many parts that were hard for me to read and made me angry but overall I did like it. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426019307i/13963325.jpg" width="250" height="350" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>See that picture of my Confess paperback up there with all the orange sticky-notes? Half of them bookmarked a scene where I was about to chuck the book at my wall because the characters were so frustrating or I didn’t see eye to eye with their actions. But the other half highlighted quotes that made me smile, and the exquisite artwork that was integral to the story. So half-half but now that I’ve had about a day to process things my feelings are not <i>that</i> torn, which is why I could bring myself to rate it rather than leave a blank for the rating.<br><br>I’ll start positive. With every Colleen Hoover book there’ll be a unique aspect to it that’s never been done before in her previous works. In Slammed it was slam poetry. In Maybe Someday it was music. And in Confess it’s artwork. This aspect is probably my favorite part because in the context of the book, the art adds a depth to the story and is a big reason why Auburn and Owen connect so deeply. The writing flowed well, and it’s easy to get sucked up in the story. I also loved that the author included real-life confessions, some that truly warmed my heart and others that made me tear up a little. And then there were definitely a few scenes that were moving and ones that had me smiling. That – for now – is probably the extent of what I loved about this book.<br><br>Now there was also a lot about the book that didn’t work for me, number 1 being I didn’t really like Auburn or Owen individually, and I never felt their romantic connection when they were a couple. But Owen first. I can’t pinpoint it exactly but from the beginning his character got on my nerves. He was so aloof and unapproachable in my eyes. This book is written in dual POVs, so in the first chapter that I got to hear his thoughts, he came off as a judgmental perfectionist.<br><br><b>
  <i>“I hope Auburn isn’t like Hannah [his ex-girlfriend]. There were so many things I didn’t like about her…Hannah disappointed me when she spoke, which is why we spent a lot of our time together not speaking.”</i>
</b><br><br>I’m sorry but that up there? Not the best first impression of a hero I’m supposed to connect with. I feel like people need to impress him and have to connect with his art for him to accept that person at all, so his character felt standoff-ish to me and I already wanted to emotionally distance myself from him. And while later on some of his actions were heroic and made me feel a little better about him, he didn’t particularly stand out as a hero to me. My overall thoughts about him are just meh.<br><br>Then there’s Auburn. Before I can explain to you why her character eventually drove me up a wall, I have to mention something else about this book. You see, there’s an extra hidden layer to this story that’s not mentioned anywhere (for good reason of course) and it’s supposed to be enough to justify why Auburn sacrifices her future and her happiness. I’ve never been in her shoes so I really wouldn’t know how authentic her situation is portrayed but it makes her romance with Owen forbidden, and with that comes a bunch of character stupidity and conflict that made me want to throw my book at the wall. I like that Auburn is a sweet, gentle and kind-hearted heroine, but I <b>
  <u>NEEDED</u>
</b> her to stand up for herself more and fight for what she wanted and not always give in. She wasn’t exactly a doormat but gosh, her indecisiveness truly frustrated me.<br><br>And then there’s Auburn and Owen’s romantic connection, which I never felt in the first place and even now that I’ve finished the book their bond still feels weak to me. The book timeline runs a couple of months but because of side character interference (I can’t say what exactly without spoiling) the total amount of time they actually spend with each other is ONE WEEK. Honestly, I think their relationship got heavy and intense way too fast and even with this author’s stellar and evocative words I still didn’t feel that special spark that both Auburn and Owen claimed they felt. <br><br>At this point with all of these things I wasn’t fond of, because of how truly amazing the book flow, the writing, the artwork, and the confessions were, I could still see myself giving this book 3.5 or 4 stars because nowhere here did I completely dislike any part of the story. However, there were 2 things that happened later on that made me go WTF and dragged down my rating considerably. They’re both HUGE spoilers though and I’m not articulate enough to explain without including them so read at your own risk here...<br><br><u>
  <b>Number 1</b>
</u><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So there’s this side character Trey who is obsessed over Auburn and he’s not afraid to use her weakness against her to get what he wants. In one particular night, he’s absolutely livid that Auburn slept with Owen and nearly RAPES her and Auburn doesn’t even fight it. She thought there for a moment that she should just let him take what he wants so he can forgive her for sleeping with Owen (what the hell is that) and after saying no a few times just collapses, sobs, and doesn’t EVEN TRY TO FIGHT HIM OFF. Forget Trey, in that one moment I wish I could be a book character, enter Confess and punch her face and tell her to have some dignity and self-respect. If it weren’t for her kickass roommate she’d have ended up as a statistic rather than a survivor. <br><br>Oh but that’s not even the best part yet. Because when the story is over, this issue is never addressed again and the blasé way the author just skips over this infuriates me. Trey isn’t punished for his actions at all. Auburn just says whatever and forgets about it. What kind of message does this send out? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><u>
  <b>Number 2</b>
</u><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[This issue is about Owen’s secret where apparently the confession is worse than the sin. I think this part I need some clarification about because this ‘secret’ of his can only refer to 2 things:<br><br>1. His situation with his Dad about taking the blame for possession and hiding it from Auburn<br>2. Him knowing about Adam (Auburn’s first love) and how Auburn’s painting factors into all this, along with Adam’s confession slip<br><br>I’m really underwhelmed here because if his big secret was #1, the blurb is exaggerating. She figures it out about halfway through the story and it didn’t even destroy their relationship; she loved him anyway. And if the big secret was #2, I feel like it’s another exaggeration. It’s not so bad that he couldn’t confess it to her because I seriously don’t see how that alone could destroy their relationship. But in the end I guess my opinion doesn’t really matter because he NEVER confessed it to her anyways, which is just ironic and goes against the theme of this book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>That’s pretty much the gist of things. In the past I wholeheartedly put my faith and trust in this author and would dive right in to her books without hesitation but her recent works Ugly Love and now this book have personally left me mindboggled. Her characters are so unlikeable (for me that is) and certain plot twists leave me more frustrated than wowed. The only constant is that her writing is beautiful and gripping as always, and will probably be the reason why I will always read her books. Maybe there’s a change in her approach to NA? Or maybe I’ve become more jaded and cynical and can’t accept how she addresses sensitive issues and ties up loose ends in her stories? Either way, I’m sad that her books aren’t appealing to me as much as they were before. This book wasn’t a total fluke for me, and when I weighed all the positive with all the negative, scraping 3 stars is still good in my eyes. I liked it yes, but it’s not a book I’m eager to recommend to everyone.<br><br><u>Confess</u> is a NA second chance romance standalone unrelated to this author’s other books.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="11903215425086248477" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1205216970" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1205216970" />
    <a title="Dorreh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh"><img alt="Dorreh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565727363p2/22599584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1205216970?book_show_action=true">Apr 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dorreh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dorreh" href="/user/show/22599584-dorreh">Dorreh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781476791456" href="/book/show/22609310-confess">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1205216970" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14529602760467110937">"There are people you meet that you get to know, and then there are people you meet that you already know."<br/><br/>A 4 hour sitting, that's how long it took me to finish this! I just couldn't put it down. <br/>I'm honestly not that big on contemporary, they usually dwell on the illusion of reality every hopeless romantic day dreams when they have a tediously long lecture or some other form of every day responsibility they couldn't spare the required attention. So I tend to lean more towards fantasy, things I</span>
  <span id="freeText14529602760467110937" style="display:none">"There are people you meet that you get to know, and then there are people you meet that you already know."<br /><br />A 4 hour sitting, that's how long it took me to finish this! I just couldn't put it down. <br />I'm honestly not that big on contemporary, they usually dwell on the illusion of reality every hopeless romantic day dreams when they have a tediously long lecture or some other form of every day responsibility they couldn't spare the required attention. So I tend to lean more towards fantasy, things I know are so simply surreal that indulge my habits of fantasizing about the impossible. <br /><br />So I really want to give Colleen Hoover a standing ovation for a book, that while dwells on the most perfect scenarios, quells such a compelling argument of reality, that one simply surrenders. Everything was pitch perfect, but you just couldn't help but love these perfect perfections. I wanted to dive into the characters and never resurface. While there were parts of Owens 'deserving' beliefs that irritated me, he was such an adorably broken-hearted puppy that I simply couldn't bring myself to truly place any dislike for him.<br /><br />I usually disagree with the portrayal of teen pregnancy as a simple issue. It tends to give teenagers the impression that things will work out even if they are careless in their relationships and decisions. So I guess my only complaint is that while Colleen Hoover works to depict a dedicated loving teenage mother who pays the price of loving her child with all the hardships and things she has given up, I personally felt the burden of unplanned motherhood is not portrayed sharply enough. <br /><br />Overall the book was intriguing, it drops you into a middle of a whirlpool where you have no choice but to surrender to being sucked in. After the epilogue, it plunged into the middle of story that we knew next to nothing of, like where it had started and where it would end. It had a tinge of mystery that makes the people who are shamelessly curious pave through the pages at the Gods pace, to get where we finally understand what in the name of heavens is actually going on. <br /><br />This was my first Colleen Hoover novel, it definitely won't be the last!!!!!<br /><br />finishing two painful books in one day, that has to be some new record of self torture.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14529602760467110937" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1837009113" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15642336174458916696">If this is Colleen Hoover's example of many people's "not my favorite book of hers" I can only imagine the treat I'm in store for. Despite others not connecting with this one so much I loved it! I fell hard for Auburn and Owen which was clearly visible by the fact I read the entire book today. While the ending was a little tidy and "too perfect", it didn't stop me from enjoying reading this one. I particularly loved the artwork included in the story and the idea behind confession inspired painti</span>
  <span id="freeText15642336174458916696" style="display:none">If this is Colleen Hoover's example of many people's "not my favorite book of hers" I can only imagine the treat I'm in store for. Despite others not connecting with this one so much I loved it! I fell hard for Auburn and Owen which was clearly visible by the fact I read the entire book today. While the ending was a little tidy and "too perfect", it didn't stop me from enjoying reading this one. I particularly loved the artwork included in the story and the idea behind confession inspired paintings. <br /><br />The story is fairly short and the characters are fairly surface level, but the author did a great job of having me root for Owen/Auburn and disliking Trey/Lydia. This book was also surprisingly tame for a romance novel; it almost had a YA feel to it and seemed more modest than some I've read recently, so this would be a good option for those looking for a cleaner love story. Really excited to read more from CoHo and am glad I picked this up from the library on a whim! </span>

          </span>
